<rating>5</rating>< Review>
Just went to Arcana Brewing after a friend recommended it to me. My boyfriend had enjoyed some of their beer at a beer and mead festival in 2019 but other than that it was completely new to us. I am so glad that our friends recommended it otherwise I wouldn‚Äôt have known how close it was to my house. The beer was absolutely amazing. They have a great selection including some unique options. We started with a flight and then got some pints. The owner was very personable and kind. He was clearly passionate and supportive of other local businesses. With over 200 breweries in San Diego County, it is great to find a location with amazing beer, service, and prices so close to home. The hours are minimal due to COVID, but I will happily make time to stop by again. The beer and service is without a doubt 100% worth it. Thank you Dan for your hospitality and service. We had a great time and will definitely be coming back.<//Review>

Arcana is the best brewery! Dan, the owner and brewer, makes really great beer as well as make every customer feel welcome. < Review>
Best beer, best host, best brewer. That's saying a lot in a region (San Diego County) that has some 120 breweries; Arcana doesn't offer a shi-shi restaurant or a fancy decor... just a really good array of beers served by the guy who owns the place and brews the brews. Dan is a great host who cares about your experience. Visit this place and compare it against breweries less authentic.</Review>

Fantastically unique beer selection and very friendly staff, with great beer prices - you can get tasters, half pours, or pints, and a flight of 4 tasters of any of their beers will put you back $8
Highly recommend the Black Magic Braggot - very flavorful, and tastes closer to mead than ale.

<rate>5<//rate><text>Of all the North County nanobreweries I've visited, Arcana consistently pours the tastiest beers. Marley's Ghost, Voyager, Headbasher, very solid top-notch brews. Sure you can find novelty beers and off-the-wall ingredients in other establishments, but after a few sips you'll likely say "next!". There isn't a beer on Arcana's board that I wouldn't drink a whole pint of.

Arcana does not hold a monopoly on great atmosphere and knowledgeable staff, but what sets them apart is the steady high-quality & taste of each individual beer. Never an off-flavor or an overbearing note, but plenty of delightful English-style ales, braggots, Belgians, and darks.< /text><response>None< /response><username>Kent Crandall< /username><Pictures>None</Pictures>< gmapID>

< Text>
This is how they work :
1) THEY LIE advertising cheap prices and unlimited mileage on the website making you come to their place.
2) They charge you $25 insurance per day (you can buy $11 insurance on Priceline) + $20 for unlimited mileage per day.
3) You can drive only in California, Nevada, Arizona + few more restrictions (see images below)
4) They charge you a huge cleaning fee and more, look at their rating there is a reason for that, read reviews, and be smarter, do NOT go there, they will find a way to charge you. Find any rental car company with a rating above 3.5 stars.

I went to Priceline to book a car as I usually do every month for 1 year, saw those very attractive prices with UNLIMITED MILES (image 5) from an unknown company Economy/Priceless "hmmm I'll give it a chance" car is booked. A few days later my schedule is set, I'm excited to go to the rental place which is hard to find on the top floor of the parking with no signs.
First red flag - a woman in line in front of me started yelling because the rental company going to charge her $150  for dog hairs on the back seat. I thought wow poor woman, vacuum cost like $3 on a car wash but I don't have a dog so I'm okay.
In my turn, the employee asked me Driver License, Credit Card, and insurance, after he filled up all the info he saying that I have 10 (TEN, X) miles per day. What!? What are you talking about man? I booked a car with unlimited miles (image 5), keep 10 miles for yourself, and just give me a car I'm in rush. Then he explained to me that I was supposed to ignore "UNLIMITED MILEAGE"  and read tiny signs after I scrolled down somewhere on the website". I told him that there was no such sign when I booked a car via Priceline. Eventually, he was trying to charge me $20 per day for unlimited miles + $22 insurance per day on top of the rental price. When I asked him "How would you feel if you're in rush, you have a schedule, you booked a car with unlimited miles but instead, you get 10 miles per day, do you think is it normal?" He answered: "it is a little harsh".</Text>

The place is easy to find inside the hotel. The only problem was getting on the shuttle for the airport pickup.
The shuttle bus has logos of many hotels printed on its body but the Renaissance hotel logo. This made us ask many shuttle drivers if they were going to the Renaissance hotel.
When we arrived to LAX, there was some shooting and some huge traffic. A shuttle driver from another hotel agreed to take us close to the Renaissance hotel due to the huge traffic, so we had to walk the rest of the way to the hotel.
The check-in process with Priceless was somewhat smooth. We were given a nice compact car which we really enjoyed.
Once we brought the car back, a lady inspected it and made sure it did not suffer from any damage. It was also a smooth process and did not take long.
We chose to use our debit car and made a deposit there. The deposit was returned to our account fairly quickly after returning the vehicle.
For the price we paid, I am so happy with the received service despite all the negative reviews on Google Maps.</Review>

Avoid this place.  First of all, the place is impossible to find.  You have to walk through the lobby of the Renaissance Hotel to the parking garage elevator, go to the top floor, and there they are.  No signs anywhere.  Then, they wanted proof of insurance - make sure you bring that if you end up renting through them.  Now, here comes the fraud.  When I booked the car, it clearly stated that I got unlimited mileage.  When I got to the location, after wasting a half an hour getting my insurance company to email coverage details to Priceless, the lady at the desk informed me that I get 100 miles per day with the reservation.  Not unlimited miles.  She said that the reason for limited miles is that I was considered a "local" renter and that I would thus not get unlimited miles.  I went back to check the terms and conditions on the Orbitz website (where I booked) and it said nothing about this.  More importantly, I'm not a local renter.  I have a California driver's license, but I do not live in the Los Angeles area.  I explained all this, and the woman demanded that I produce a boarding pass.  I showed her evidence that I was flying out of LAX in a couple weeks' time, but she wanted to see a boarding pass that showed that I was on an airplane today.  Bottom line, this place advertises very low prices, but it's in incredible inconvenience to use them.  They bait and switch - advertising unlimited mileage but not actually offering it.  I would highly recommend renting a car from a more established and reputable outlet.< /text>

Super fun area! My bf and I actually never found the arch rock because we got so distracted by all the rock formations on the way. Embarrassing, I know, but we had a blast exploring and climbing around the rocks. Coming around every corner and angle gave unique and stunning views. We‚Äôll just have to come back to find the arch and try not to get too distracted. We ran into other hikers who couldn‚Äôt find it either, so it seems like this may be a common phenomenon.

Also, for bathrooms, go to the nearby white tank campground.<//review>

Arch Rock Nature Trail is a fun place. There's a parking lot nearby. The trail is fairly well marked. Arch Rock doesn't stand out right away. You have to read the signs. It wasn't as big of an arch as what I thought it was going to be. Wear good shoes or hiking boots, as there are rocks and boulders to climb on. Great views too!<//text>

<userid>103663667069797423399<//userid>< user_name>
Warren Hoo<//user_name>
<date>1597978740829<//date><rating>5</rating>< Review>
Awesome mind boggling sight to see humongous sized boulders piled together.  Boulders are a medium course sand composition that provides grippy surface for climbing. The walk from the parking lot is easy.  The last section necessary to access and see the Arch Rock formation is of medium difficulty if you're in decent physical condition. Older Elementary age children likely need to be strong and agile.  Some areas require a squeeze through. Much of the last leg to access and see the Arch Rock face on requires climbing.  Doable with flip flops which I wore.  Shoes are much safer for mounting up onto rounded boulders. A 24mm lens on a full frame 36mm camera can capture the Arch Rock. A panorama of three horizontal widths with the 24 mm lens is impressive. If walking in the August 100+¬∞F heat,  a nice broad rim hat and sunglasses help.   Bring and drink lots of water.</Review>

<Review>It's been 3 months since my roommate and I moved into our 2-bedroom, 1-bath, and we've both been loving it. The apartment is spacious and welcoming after a long day of work. Both of us appreciate the little things such as:
- There is carpet in the bedrooms, while the rest of the apartment is tiled. The carpet not only makes the bedroom more comfortable, but it also helps cut down on the noise from downstairs neighbors.
- There is a solid wood door that pulls out of the wall in order to separate the living room and kitchen from the bedrooms. We were both pleasantly surprised with how much it cuts down on the noise between the areas. I can be gaming at a normal volume in the living room while my roommate can still sleep peacefully.
- There is a sink/counter/mirror setup in the master bedroom. This cuts down on time waiting to use the bathroom to get ready in the morning. My roommate just hops out of the shower and gets ready all in the master bedroom.

One main thing that we really like is the responsiveness from the office staff on property. We had put in a maintenance request to rehang the bedroom mirror that fell off the wall. After a couple days we were getting a little impatient, but once we reached out to Jason Vazquez, from the leasing office, he got the ball rolling. The mirror was rehung by the end of the day.
Jason also helped us with the process of actually renting the place. Being that it was my roommate and I's first time renting our own place, we had plenty of questions. Jason never tried to persuade me when I visited for the first time, but instead was very informative and educational regarding all the ins-and-outs. Jason was incredibly helpful and made the whole experience much less of a struggle than it could've been. If it‚Äôs your first time renting, I highly recommend getting in contact with him.

I would recommend this anybody looking for a good quality, basic apartment. Our stairwell neighbors are from all different walks of life but have always been courteous and friendly. This has been a great starter apartment for both of us!< /Review>< response>

< review>
Decent place for a decent price. The newly renovated apartments are visually pleasing, but we've had a few issues with things here or there (fridge/freezer shutting off since the outlet was fried, towel rack falling off, cockroaches, heating panel not working, wood floor paneling coming up to cite a few). The facilities team is helpful but I'd recommend submitting online then calling to get things done quickly. You get one parking spot for a two bedroom apartment and parking tends to get rough after 6pm, so plan accordingly. The Barclay Apt team leaves paper notices between doors notifying residents of current events including the monthly water shut-off hours (not sure why this is happening). The water tends to be shut-off from 10am-2pm, though, so it shouldn't affect you much as long as you have a 8-5pm full-time job or something similar. Any noises within the apartment structure tend to echo so children/dogs(a lot of service dogs in the apartments to evade the no pets rule)/music are quite noticeable. There's often new graffiti on the back fences by the parking spaces (it's constantly getting repainted), and there are often people sorting through the garbage bins collecting things, so it's not the most private apartment complex. I will say that I've never had a bad experience with any of the strangers. Also good to note that the Fire station is just around the corner, so you'll hear the occasional fire truck siren.<//review>

Stay Away and Find Something Better! If I could give negative stars, I would given Barclay Square Apartments - and more specifically the current staff Jason and Eric at the leasing office at least negative 2. If you have looked at any of the positive reviews as some kind of reassurance before you decide to sign a lease here - don't worry, those are paid for by the leasing office through gifting.

Let's start with COCKROACHES. First let's recognize that I am referring to both the infestation of our apartment for the last 12 months and those working at the leasing office. When my husband and I originally moved in 2 years ago, there was a completely different staff, and there was not a constant influx of insects coming in through the walls, drains, and cabinets. If the question of resigning our lease had been with this current staff, we wouldn't have even considered. But the previous staff were actually sympathetic to us seeing an occasional cockroach, and promised us solutions so we did what any naive couple looking for 'affordable' rent in San Diego would do, and resigned our lease with a $250/month increase. What a mistake!

Here's where our story became a nightmare. Enter the new members of the leasing office and the increased cockroach infestation.

Did we continue to charge you last years rent with an unalterable autoplay WITHOUT NOTIFYING YOU FOR 5 MONTHS of underpaying rent and subsequently try to evict you with 3 days notice without explanation? Sounds like a leasing office with some integrity. But the integrity really becomes evident when you do pay that additional $1250 for the clerical mistake that this same new leasing office asks for. Let's talk about payment plans. The leasing office decided we could divide that $1250 of incurred expenses (from their mistake) into a payment plan for 3 months, which they would put an eviction notice (not folded) on our door, despite paying their payment plan that they set up.

But let's not get bored with money here, let's get back to the exciting prospect of cockroaches. Want a variety of carcinogenic chemicals sprayed weekly at no cost to you without actually resolving your problem of cockroaches in the walls? Look no further than Barclay Square!

Now that we have moved past the creatures, let's talk about the water shut-offs that happen weekly, with advanced notice only 50% of the time. If you're looking to commute to work without the ability to take a shower in the morning, this is your place. The best is when halfway through your shower the water gets shutoff with soap in your eyes. Brushing your teeth with bottled water is probably good for the soul, right?

Do yourself a favor, and look for apartments where the people who take your hard-earned money actually care about resolving your issues. If you're looking for apartments where when your sink is literally flooding your place, and you run to the office only to be met by a locked door at 8:58AM with someone who can see you and refuses to open the door until it is 9:00AM, than this is your place! <text>DO NOT MOVE HERE if you value sleep and your money!!!! There is a reason why there are so many vacancies here year round. They are either old units that break down frequently or they are cheaply renovated ‚Äúmodern‚Äù units with old unit problems related to plumbing, thin walls, mold, or other miscellaneous problems.

First off, the prices fluctuate daily when you first apply for a unit. Scheduling a tour of a unit you want is a coin toss - either you get to see it because the unit has been off the market for awhile or you don‚Äôt due to either necessary repairs, painting, renovations, heavy cleaning needed, or they just don‚Äôt want to show you because it isn‚Äôt ‚Äúready‚Äù to be viewed. If you see a price that‚Äôs a steal for the unit, it is first come first served; but beware - they will make you put down a holding deposit to lock in the price whether or not you were able to view the unit.

Now, onto the move-in process. If you were lucky, you got a unit that was a corner unit upstairs and didn‚Äôt need any repairs, had no pest problems, or didn‚Äôt need appliances replaced on the 1st day/week of move in. AND if you were more lucky, you have nice, quiet neighbors whom you can‚Äôt hear arguing, children crying/yelling/playing inside, dogs barking, or your neighbors‚Äô tv/music/shower/vacuum/other loud sounds at odd hours of the day/night because your walls are well-insulated from noise. If not, be prepared to deal with all sorts of problems from day one of move in. Personally, I had an initial roach problem during the first week with a few dead roaches not being cleaned out of our kitchen cabinets, roach poop build up not cleaned from the top of and the inside of the metal thing that our vertical blinds sits on (the ones leading to the balcony), and 3 stray roaches that appeared here and there in the evening(s) that I immediately exterminated with my handy, dandy, rolled-up magazine. I also thoroughly cleaned my apartment with homemade cleaner from top to bottom and especially made sure to thoroughly spot clean the entire kitchen and the area around the sliding door leading outside to our balcony after every roach sighting. Haven‚Äôt seen one since.

Other things to note about this property:
- Laundry rooms are open until 10pm, machines are often out of order in each of the laundry rooms
- 1 assigned parking space so be prepared for parking wars on the side streets after 5pm (side note: some people park illegally behind the building where the oddly one way parking lot is located on the side close to Balboa Ave without getting towed)
- Noise complaints (dogs barking all night, music playing loudly at night, etc.) will not be addressed unless you want to call the cops on your neighbors
- This is a non-smoking community on paper, not in practice so stay away if you have kids or health problems
- Homeless people dig through the trash or wash their clothes in the sink in the laundry rooms
- No A/C in the units which can be avoided if you stay away from your place on those hot summer days or buy a window A/C unit
- Water shuts off occasionally with/without notice (85% they give notice)
- A good chunk of your deposit will be gone due to painting, cleaning, etc. whatever they can muster up so fight for your deposit during pre-inspection and after you move out
- Close to shops, a fire station, 805
- Friendly maintenance staff! (Hence 2 stars)

If you were able to survive your hopefully short term leasing period that they made somewhat affordable without any of the major problems previously mentioned, congratulations!! <Date>1543461288217< /Date><rating>4</rating><Text>Unique primitive hot spring, mud bath.  water is hot about 104 degrees plus at the largest part of this marshy hot spring.  Really easy to get too, park along the road. Can be quite busy. Went on a Sunday night and there were quite a few different groups. Hot spring is large enough to have privacy with varying levels of heat. No place to sit once in the water unless is the shallower part.  Mud floor is nice to walk though but be careful of the hot spots! Overall wonderful, no odor silky soft water. Accessible 24/7, dog friendly.  Clothing optional!  Great night time soaking under the moonlight.

There are hot spring mites that will bite on you for a couple hours after,your soak but they dont leave marks.   You can see them dancing on top the water if you have good eyes.   Nice place just because there is really nothing else for free.  It get busy.   It is dangerously slippy in the mud outside the pools.   Bring a blanket and tarp to lay out between soaks.  Bring water to drink.< /Text>

< text>
I really like this place in terms of quality, portion sizes, and price! I love checking out new asian dessert sit down shops because there aren't many that I like and I am always in a hunt for more. I have heard so many good things about this place. I was so happy to finally come here with two friends.

We all ordered three items to share!

*Thai Tea Roti - The roti takes a while to make but it was worth the wait! The roti was crispy and a lot of glaze topped with it. The thai tea icecream was just perfect with it.

*Mango sticky rice crepe - This was our favorite! This came out fairly quickly too! The skin is so thin and soft. The sticky rice is in the middle or the crepe. It is a little heavy on the whip cream but it's dessert so that's ok!

*Steamed bread with pandan dip - Wasn't impressed with this one. The bread it just a slice of bread cut into piece which I feel like it was something that is easy to make at home. The picture made it look more complicated.

Overall, I really like this place! I would totally come back here. I came on a weeknight so it wasn't too busy but I can imagine this place packed during the weekend.</text>

< review>
I don't spend much time in the Inner Richmond, so I wanted to take advantage of the visit out there and go to this Na Ya location for the first time. This location is quaint and decorated in what some may call shabby chic; something I noticed right off the bat (and which may border on unsafe) is that the floor was wet and I felt my shoes sliding on it.

It wasn't busy when I arrived so my bf and I were able to be seated right away and were given menus. We ordered the mille crepe cake to share since I hadn't been able to try it before (the Hayes Valley location is alwaysss out). When it arrived, it was somewhat smaller than expected, but the way it was presented was cute. Flavour-wise, it was all right; I expected a stronger flavour after having tried mille crepe cakes at similar establishments. This one mostly just tasted like cream.

As many of the other reviewers mentioned, it's cash only - not a deal-breaker, but just something to be aware of when visiting this business. Overall, the experience was fine but I'll probably check out some other nearby businesses the next time I'm around here.</review>

<username>Jay M.< /username>< date>

<response>None<//response><user_id>107677940022869036597</user_id><Rating>1</Rating><pics>None< /pics>< review>
Let me start off saying that I am very disappointed that I can not give Na Ya a better review as my impression from the reviews online was incredible.

Upon entering, I found there to be a nicely decorated store.  I was immediately greeted a server who brought us water after presenting menus.

After ordering, we waited quite a bit for our crepes to be made.  I observed the preparer place whip cream on my crepe.  She got stopped by the server who noted that it had been ordered without whip cream.  They then proceeded in using napkins to wipe away some of the whip cream that was placed on my crepe.  To cover up the mistake, I observed the preparer add more filling.

When the beautifully presented crepe was delivered to me, I asked the server if there was any whip cream placed on it as I am highly sensitive to it.  She said no.  I then said that I saw the preparer place whip cream on it and that I had seen her to stop.  She continued to insist that none had been placed on it.

I carefully ate the crepe which was quite delicious and avoided areas that seemed to have some signs of whip cream.

When the check arrived, my guest observed that one of the crepes was a higher charge even though they were similar and should have been the same price.  I brought this up to the server who consulted one of the owner's.  She said that she would correct the error.  A correct check was delivered with no apology but only an excuse that there was something wrong with the register.

Overall, the desserts purchased were delicious, however the long wait for the food and poor customer service deem this as a place that I would never return to.<//review>
